#### The Study

Nutrients 2024, 16(3), 398; https://doi.org/10.3390/nu16030398

Carsten Carlberg 1,2,*ORCID and Eunike Velleuer 3,4ORCID

1 Institute of Animal Reproduction and Food Research, Polish Academy of Sciences, PL-10-748 Olsztyn, Poland

2 School of Medicine, Institute of Biomedicine, University of Eastern Finland, FI-70211 Kuopio, Finland

3 Department for Cytopathology, Heinrich-Heine-University DГјsseldorf, D-40225 DГјsseldorf, Germany

4 Department for Pediatric Hemato-Oncology, Helios ChildrenвЂ™s Hospital, D-47805 Krefeld, Germany

(This article belongs to the Section Nutrigenetics and Nutrigenomics)

<img src="/attachments/d3.mock.jpg" alt="image" width="500">

The pro-hormone vitamin D3 is an important modulator of both innate and adaptive immunity since its biologically active metabolite 1О±,25-dihydroxyvitamin D3 (1,25(OH)2D3) regulates via the transcription factor VDR (vitamin D receptor) the epigenome and transcriptome of human immune cells and controls in this way the expression of hundreds of vitamin D target genes. Since the myeloid linage of hematopoiesis is epigenetically programmed by VDR in concert with the pioneer factors PU.1 (purine-rich box 1) and CEBPО± (CCAAT/enhancer binding protein О±), monocytes, macrophages, and dendritic cells are the most vitamin D-sensitive immune cell types. 

The central role of the immune system in various aging-related diseases suggests that immunocompetence describes not only the ability of an individual to resist pathogens and parasites but also to contest non-communicative diseases and the process of aging itself.

In this review, we argue that the individual-specific responsiveness to vitamin D relates to a personвЂ™s immunocompetence via the epigenetic programming function of VDR and its ligand 1,25(OH)2D3 during hematopoiesis as well as in the periphery.

This may provide a mechanism explaining how vitamin D protects against major common diseases and, in parallel, promotes healthy aging.

##### Conclusion suggests daily Vitamin D3 = 40 IU/kg (3,200 IU for 80 kg adult)

 **[<i class="fas fa-file-pdf" style="margin-right: 0.3em;"></i>Download the PDF from VitaminDWiki ](/attachments/d3.mock.pdf)**

#### The Study

Nutrients 2024, 16(3), 398; https://doi.org/10.3390/nu16030398

Carsten Carlberg 1,2,*ORCID and Eunike Velleuer 3,4ORCID

1 Institute of Animal Reproduction and Food Research, Polish Academy of Sciences, PL-10-748 Olsztyn, Poland

2 School of Medicine, Institute of Biomedicine, University of Eastern Finland, FI-70211 Kuopio, Finland

3 Department for Cytopathology, Heinrich-Heine-University DГјsseldorf, D-40225 DГјsseldorf, Germany

4 Department for Pediatric Hemato-Oncology, Helios ChildrenвЂ™s Hospital, D-47805 Krefeld, Germany

(This article belongs to the Section Nutrigenetics and Nutrigenomics)

&lt;img src=&quot;/attachments/d3.mock.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;image&quot; width=&quot;500&quot;&gt;

The pro-hormone vitamin D3 is an important modulator of both innate and adaptive immunity since its biologically active metabolite 1О±,25-dihydroxyvitamin D3 (1,25(OH)2D3) regulates via the transcription factor VDR (vitamin D receptor) the epigenome and transcriptome of human immune cells and controls in this way the expression of hundreds of vitamin D target genes. Since the myeloid linage of hematopoiesis is epigenetically programmed by VDR in concert with the pioneer factors PU.1 (purine-rich box 1) and CEBPО± (CCAAT/enhancer binding protein О±), monocytes, macrophages, and dendritic cells are the most vitamin D-sensitive immune cell types. 

The central role of the immune system in various aging-related diseases suggests that immunocompetence describes not only the ability of an individual to resist pathogens and parasites but also to contest non-communicative diseases and the process of aging itself.

In this review, we argue that the individual-specific responsiveness to vitamin D relates to a personвЂ™s immunocompetence via the epigenetic programming function of VDR and its ligand 1,25(OH)2D3 during hematopoiesis as well as in the periphery.

This may provide a mechanism explaining how vitamin D protects against major common diseases and, in parallel, promotes healthy aging.

##### Conclusion suggests daily Vitamin D3 = 40 IU/kg (3,200 IU for 80 kg adult)

 **[&lt;i class=&quot;fas fa-file-pdf&quot; style=&quot;margin-right: 0.3em;&quot;&gt;&lt;/i&gt;Download the PDF from VitaminDWiki ](/attachments/d3.mock.pdf)**

Since the myeloid linage of hematopoiesis is epigenetically programmed by VDR in concert with the pioneer factors PU.1 (purine-rich box 1) and CEBPО± (CCAAT/enhancer binding protein О±), monocytes, macrophages, and dendritic cells are the most vitamin D-sensitive immune cell types. \nThe central role of the immune system in various aging-related diseases suggests that immunocompetence describes not only the ability of an individual to resist pathogens and parasites but also to contest non-communicative diseases and the process of aging itself.\nIn this review, we argue that the individual-specific responsiveness to vitamin D relates to a personвЂ™s immunocompetence via the epigenetic programming function of VDR and its ligand 1,25(OH)2D3 during hematopoiesis as well as in the periphery.\nThis may provide a mechanism explaining how vitamin D protects against major common diseases and, in parallel, promotes healthy aging.\n`

{DIV(class=&quot;lefth4&quot;)}{maketoc Title=&quot;&quot;}{DIV}
---
!!!!The Study
Nutrients 2024, 16(3), 398; https://doi.org/10.3390/nu16030398
Carsten Carlberg 1,2,*ORCID and Eunike Velleuer 3,4ORCID
1 Institute of Animal Reproduction and Food Research, Polish Academy of Sciences, PL-10-748 Olsztyn, Poland
2 School of Medicine, Institute of Biomedicine, University of Eastern Finland, FI-70211 Kuopio, Finland
3 Department for Cytopathology, Heinrich-Heine-University DГјsseldorf, D-40225 DГјsseldorf, Germany
4 Department for Pediatric Hemato-Oncology, Helios ChildrenвЂ™s Hospital, D-47805 Krefeld, Germany

(This article belongs to the Section Nutrigenetics and Nutrigenomics)
{img type=&quot;attId&quot; attId=&quot;21008&quot; width=&quot;500&quot;}

The pro-hormone vitamin D3 is an important modulator of both innate and adaptive immunity since its biologically active metabolite 1О±,25-dihydroxyvitamin D3 (1,25(OH)2D3) regulates via the transcription factor VDR (vitamin D receptor) the epigenome and transcriptome of human immune cells and controls in this way the expression of hundreds of vitamin D target genes. Since the myeloid linage of hematopoiesis is epigenetically programmed by VDR in concert with the pioneer factors PU.1 (purine-rich box 1) and CEBPО± (CCAAT/enhancer binding protein О±), monocytes, macrophages, and dendritic cells are the most vitamin D-sensitive immune cell types. 
The central role of the immune system in various aging-related diseases suggests that immunocompetence describes not only the ability of an individual to resist pathogens and parasites but also to contest non-communicative diseases and the process of aging itself.
In this review, we argue that the individual-specific responsiveness to vitamin D relates to a personвЂ™s immunocompetence via the epigenetic programming function of VDR and its ligand 1,25(OH)2D3 during hematopoiesis as well as in the periphery.
This may provide a mechanism explaining how vitamin D protects against major common diseases and, in parallel, promotes healthy aging.
!!!!!Conclusion suggests daily Vitamin D3 = 40 IU/kg (3,200 IU for 80 kg adult)
{FONT(size=&quot;18&quot;)}__{ATTACH(inline=&quot;1&quot; id=&quot;21007&quot; icon=&quot;1&quot;)}Download the PDF from VitaminDWiki {ATTACH}__{FONT}
